## Chapter: Brownfields Policy and Practice: A Comprehensive Guide to Urban Redevelopment

### Introduction

In the previous chapters, we have explored the concept of brownfields, their characteristics, and the various policies and practices that have been implemented to address them. We have also delved into the challenges faced by stakeholders in the redevelopment process and the strategies they employ to overcome these obstacles. In this chapter, we will focus on the role of stakeholders in brownfield redevelopment, examining their responsibilities, challenges, and strategies in more detail.

Stakeholders play a crucial role in brownfield redevelopment. They are the individuals, groups, or organizations that have a vested interest in the redevelopment process. These can include property owners, developers, government agencies, community groups, and environmental consultants. Each stakeholder brings their own unique perspective and set of concerns to the table, making collaboration and communication among them essential for successful redevelopment.

This chapter will explore the various roles and responsibilities of stakeholders in brownfield redevelopment. We will discuss the challenges they face, such as funding constraints, regulatory requirements, and community opposition. We will also examine the strategies they employ to overcome these challenges, such as public-private partnerships, innovative financing mechanisms, and community engagement.

By understanding the role of stakeholders in brownfield redevelopment, we can gain a deeper appreciation for the complexities of the process and the importance of collaboration among all parties involved. This chapter aims to provide a comprehensive guide to navigating the intricate web of stakeholders in brownfield redevelopment, equipping readers with the knowledge and tools necessary to successfully navigate this process.

## Chapter: Brownfields Policy and Practice: A Comprehensive Guide to Urban Redevelopment

### Introduction

In the previous chapters, we have explored the concept of brownfields, their characteristics, and the various policies and practices that have been implemented to address them. We have also delved into the challenges faced by stakeholders in the redevelopment process and the strategies they employ to overcome these obstacles. In this chapter, we will focus on the role of stakeholders in brownfield redevelopment, examining their responsibilities, challenges, and strategies in more detail.

Stakeholders play a crucial role in brownfield redevelopment. They are the individuals, groups, or organizations that have a vested interest in the redevelopment process. These can include property owners, developers, government agencies, community groups, and environmental consultants. Each stakeholder brings their own unique perspective and set of concerns to the table, making collaboration and communication among them essential for successful redevelopment.

This chapter will explore the various roles and responsibilities of stakeholders in brownfield redevelopment. We will discuss the challenges they face, such as funding constraints, regulatory requirements, and community opposition. We will also examine the strategies they employ to overcome these challenges, such as public-private partnerships, innovative financing mechanisms, and community engagement.

By understanding the role of stakeholders in brownfield redevelopment, we can gain a deeper appreciation for the complexities of the process and the importance of collaboration among all parties involved. This chapter aims to provide a comprehensive guide to navigating the intricate web of stakeholders in brownfield redevelopment, equipping readers with the knowledge and tools necessary to successfully navigate this process.




### Introduction

In this chapter, we will be taking a closer look at the City of Lynn, a bustling urban area known for its rich history and diverse culture. The city has been a hub of industrial activity for over a century, with numerous factories and mills operating within its boundaries. However, as with many other industrial cities, the City of Lynn has also faced the challenges of urban decay and environmental contamination.

The City of Lynn is a prime example of the concept of brownfields, which are abandoned or underutilized properties that have been contaminated by hazardous substances. These properties, often located in urban areas, pose significant health and environmental risks to nearby communities. The City of Lynn, like many other brownfield sites, has a complex history of industrial use and subsequent contamination.

In this chapter, we will explore the history of the City of Lynn, its current state, and the efforts being made to revitalize and redevelop the area. We will also discuss the various policies and practices that have been implemented to address the environmental and health concerns associated with brownfields. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a comprehensive understanding of the challenges and opportunities presented by brownfields, and the importance of sustainable urban redevelopment.




### Section: 5.1 Overview of Lynn's Brownfields:

The City of Lynn, located in Massachusetts, USA, is a prime example of a city facing the challenges of urban decay and environmental contamination. With a rich history of industrial activity, the city has been home to numerous factories and mills, many of which have since been abandoned or underutilized. These properties, known as brownfields, pose significant health and environmental risks to nearby communities.

### Subsection: 5.1a History of Lynn's Industrial Sites

The City of Lynn has a long history of industrial activity, dating back to the 19th century when it was a major center of textile production. The city's strategic location, with easy access to raw materials and transportation routes, made it an ideal location for industrial development. However, as the textile industry declined in the late 19th and early 20th centuries, many of the city's factories and mills were abandoned or repurposed for other industrial uses.

One of the most significant industrial sites in Lynn is the former Bethlehem Steel plant, which was established in 1861 and operated until 1995. The plant was a major producer of steel and other metal products, employing thousands of workers and contributing significantly to the city's economy. However, as the steel industry declined in the late 20th century, the plant was closed and left abandoned, leaving behind a contaminated site that posed significant environmental and health risks.

The Bethlehem Steel plant is just one example of the many industrial sites in Lynn that have been abandoned or underutilized. These sites, known as brownfields, are often contaminated with hazardous substances such as heavy metals, petroleum, and pesticides, which can have serious health impacts on nearby communities. The City of Lynn has been proactive in addressing these brownfields, implementing various policies and practices to revitalize and redevelop these sites.

### Subsection: 5.1b Environmental Contamination at Lynn's Brownfields

The environmental contamination at Lynn's brownfields is a significant concern for the city and its residents. The abandoned and underutilized industrial sites have been left with a legacy of pollution, which can have serious health impacts on nearby communities. The contamination is often caused by the release of hazardous substances during industrial processes, such as the production of steel and other metal products.

One of the most common types of contamination at Lynn's brownfields is soil and groundwater contamination. The release of hazardous substances into the soil and groundwater can have long-lasting effects, making the land unsuitable for future development. In addition, the contamination can also seep into nearby water bodies, such as rivers and lakes, posing a threat to aquatic life and potentially contaminating drinking water sources.

### Subsection: 5.1c Community Impact of Lynn's Brownfields

The environmental contamination at Lynn's brownfields has had a significant impact on the surrounding communities. The presence of hazardous substances can lead to a range of health issues, including respiratory illnesses, skin diseases, and even cancer. In addition, the contamination can also have economic impacts, as it can decrease property values and limit job opportunities in the area.

The City of Lynn has been proactive in addressing the community impact of its brownfields. The city has implemented various policies and practices to revitalize and redevelop these sites, including brownfield cleanup and redevelopment programs, as well as community engagement and education initiatives. These efforts aim to not only address the environmental contamination but also to improve the quality of life for the city's residents.

### Subsection: 5.1d Future Plans for Lynn's Brownfields

The City of Lynn has a long-term plan to address its brownfields, with the goal of revitalizing and redeveloping these sites for future use. The city has identified several key strategies for achieving this goal, including:

- Continued cleanup and redevelopment of brownfield sites, with a focus on creating mixed-use developments that include residential, commercial, and recreational spaces.
- Implementation of green infrastructure and sustainable design practices to mitigate the environmental impacts of redevelopment.
- Collaboration with local businesses and community organizations to create job opportunities and support economic growth in the area.
- Ongoing community engagement and education efforts to keep residents informed and involved in the brownfield redevelopment process.

The City of Lynn's efforts to address its brownfields serve as a model for other cities facing similar challenges. By implementing comprehensive policies and practices, Lynn has shown that it is possible to revitalize and redevelop these sites, improving the health and well-being of its residents and creating a more sustainable future for the city.





### Subsection: 5.1b Current State of Lynn's Brownfields

The City of Lynn has made significant progress in addressing its brownfields, but there is still much work to be done. The current state of Lynn's brownfields can be categorized into three main areas: active redevelopment, ongoing assessment, and future potential.

#### Active Redevelopment

There are several brownfield sites in Lynn that are currently undergoing redevelopment. One of the most notable is the former Bethlehem Steel plant, which is being transformed into a mixed-use development with residential, commercial, and recreational spaces. The project, known as Steel & Darling, is expected to create over 1,000 jobs and bring new life to the area.

Another active redevelopment project is the former Lynn Mills site, which is being transformed into a new industrial park. The project, known as Lynn Industrial Park, will provide much-needed space for new businesses and create jobs in the city.

#### Ongoing Assessment

There are also several brownfield sites in Lynn that are currently being assessed for potential redevelopment. These sites are being evaluated for their environmental conditions and potential for redevelopment. One such site is the former Lynn Manufacturing Company site, which is being considered for a potential mixed-use development.

#### Future Potential

In addition to the active redevelopment and ongoing assessment projects, there are many brownfield sites in Lynn that have yet to be fully assessed for their potential for redevelopment. These sites represent a significant opportunity for future development and revitalization in the city.

Overall, the current state of Lynn's brownfields is one of progress and potential. With continued efforts and investment, the city can continue to transform its brownfields into valuable assets for the community.

```
# Scarborough Town Centre

## Proposed development

Currently, multiple plans are proposed for the shopping mall and its surroundings.

### Scarborough Subway Extension

The extension of TTC's Line 2 Bloor-Danforth subway line is currently under construction, which will extend the line 7.8 kilometers. The extension will start from Kennedy station and go north towards McCowan Road and Sheppard Avenue with a station at the centre. This will replace the current Line 3 Scarborough that passes through the centre. The extension is expected to be complete around 2030.

### Redevelopment of the centre

A proposal was created by Oxford Properties to redevelop the centre. For the first phase, the existing Cineplex Cinemas would be demolished to create space for the subway extension to the mall and a new transit hub. The current theatre would be replaced with a new movie theatre adjacent to the former Sears location. The Sears location would be renovated and divided into at least 18 retail units with three levels. A pedestrian walkway will connect the mall with the new movie theatre # Birkenhead

## Future

The major redevelopment project under consideration is Peel Holdings' "Wirral Waters". This would allow for £4.5 billion of investment in the regeneration of the dockland area. This equates with an investment of over £14,000 for each of the 320,000 residents of the Wirral. At the East Float and Vittoria Dock, the development would include of new office space and for new residential flats. A retail and leisure quarter at the former Bidston Dock site would encompass another of space. The whole project would create more than 27,000 permanent new jobs, aside from the employment required for construction and other peripheral employment. The development would be expected to take up to thirty years # METRORapid Silver Line

## Expansion

An extension north to Northwest Mall—a future Texas Central Railway station)—and a western extension to the Hillcroft Transit Center have been proposed. This would allow for a more efficient and convenient transportation system for the city. The expansion is still in the planning stages and is expected to be completed in the next few years.

```

### Subsection: 5.1c Future Plans for Redevelopment

The City of Lynn has made significant progress in addressing its brownfields, but there is still much work to be done. The future plans for redevelopment in Lynn are focused on creating a more sustainable and livable community for its residents.

#### Sustainable Development

One of the key goals of the City of Lynn is to promote sustainable development. This includes incorporating green spaces and sustainable design features into new developments. The city has also implemented policies to encourage the use of renewable energy sources and reduce carbon emissions.

#### Mixed-Use Development

The City of Lynn is also looking to increase the diversity of its economy by promoting mixed-use development. This includes creating more opportunities for retail, office, and residential spaces in the city. The redevelopment of the former Bethlehem Steel plant and the Lynn Mills site are examples of this, as they will provide a mix of uses and create new job opportunities.

#### Public Spaces

In addition to creating more green spaces, the City of Lynn is also looking to improve its public spaces. This includes revitalizing existing parks and creating new ones, as well as improving sidewalks and bike lanes to encourage more active transportation. The redevelopment of the former Lynn Manufacturing Company site is a prime example of this, as it will include a new public park and pedestrian-friendly design.

#### Affordable Housing

The City of Lynn is also facing a shortage of affordable housing, and the redevelopment of brownfields presents an opportunity to address this issue. The city has implemented policies to encourage the inclusion of affordable housing units in new developments, and the redevelopment of the former Bethlehem Steel plant will include affordable housing units.

#### Economic Development

The City of Lynn is also looking to attract new businesses and create job opportunities. The redevelopment of brownfields can help to revitalize the local economy and create new job opportunities. The City of Lynn has also established a Brownfields Redevelopment Fund to provide financial incentives for developers to redevelop brownfields.

#### Community Engagement

The City of Lynn is committed to involving the community in the redevelopment process. The city has established a Brownfields Redevelopment Advisory Committee to provide input and feedback on redevelopment plans. The city also holds public meetings and workshops to gather input from the community.

In conclusion, the future plans for redevelopment in Lynn are focused on creating a more sustainable, diverse, and livable community for its residents. By incorporating sustainable development, mixed-use development, public spaces, affordable housing, economic development, and community engagement, the City of Lynn is working towards a brighter future for its residents.





#### Conclusion

The City of Lynn, located in Massachusetts, USA, serves as a prime example of successful urban redevelopment through the implementation of brownfield policies and practices. This chapter has provided a comprehensive overview of the city's history, current state, and future plans, highlighting the key role of brownfield redevelopment in its transformation.

The city's history is steeped in industrial activity, with a rich tapestry of manufacturing and production. However, the decline of these industries led to a significant number of brownfield sites, posing environmental and economic challenges. The city's response to these challenges has been exemplary, demonstrating a commitment to sustainable urban development.

The city's brownfield redevelopment efforts have been guided by a comprehensive policy framework, which has facilitated the cleanup and reuse of these sites. The policy framework has been complemented by a range of practices, including public-private partnerships, innovative financing mechanisms, and community engagement. These practices have not only addressed the environmental and economic challenges posed by brownfields but have also contributed to the city's overall revitalization.

Looking ahead, the City of Lynn is poised for further redevelopment, with a focus on creating a more livable and sustainable urban environment. The city's brownfield policy and practice serve as a model for other urban areas grappling with similar challenges. The lessons learned from Lynn's experience can inform future brownfield redevelopment efforts, contributing to the broader goal of sustainable urban development.

These practices have not only addressed the environmental and economic challenges posed by brownfields but have also contributed to the city's overall revitalization.

Looking ahead, the City of Lynn is poised for further redevelopment, with a focus on creating a more livable and sustainable urban environment. The city's brownfield policy and practice serve as a model for other urban areas grappling with similar challenges. The lessons learned from Lynn's experience can inform future brownfield redevelopment efforts, contributing to the broader goal of sustainable urban development.

### Introduction

In this chapter, we will explore the intersection of brownfields redevelopment and environmental justice and equity. Brownfields, defined as abandoned or underutilized properties with potential environmental contamination, are often located in urban areas and have a disproportionate impact on marginalized communities. The redevelopment of these properties has the potential to bring economic and social benefits, but it also raises important questions about fairness and equity.

We will begin by examining the concept of environmental justice and its relevance to brownfields redevelopment. Environmental justice is a social movement that seeks to address the unequal distribution of environmental benefits and burdens, particularly among marginalized communities. Brownfields, with their history of industrial use and potential contamination, are often located in these communities, making them a key focus of the environmental justice movement.

Next, we will delve into the concept of equity in brownfields redevelopment. Equity refers to fairness and justice in the distribution of benefits and burdens. In the context of brownfields, equity is crucial as these properties have the potential to bring significant benefits, such as job creation and improved property values, to surrounding communities. However, if these benefits are not equitably distributed, it can exacerbate existing inequalities and further marginalize already disadvantaged communities.

Throughout this chapter, we will explore the various policies and practices that have been implemented to address environmental justice and equity in brownfields redevelopment. These include federal and state laws, as well as community-based initiatives and partnerships. We will also examine case studies and best practices to gain a deeper understanding of how these policies and practices are being implemented in real-world scenarios.

By the end of this chapter, readers will have a comprehensive understanding of the complex and multifaceted issues surrounding environmental justice and equity in brownfields redevelopment. This knowledge will be essential for anyone involved in the planning, implementation, or evaluation of brownfields redevelopment projects, as well as for those interested in the broader social and environmental implications of these projects. 





### Subsection: 6.1a Definition of Environmental Justice

Environmental justice is a concept that has gained significant attention in recent years, particularly in the context of brownfields redevelopment. It is a social movement that seeks to address the unequal distribution of environmental benefits and burdens, particularly among marginalized communities. In this section, we will explore the definition of environmental justice and its relevance to brownfields redevelopment.

Environmental justice is typically defined as distributive justice, which is "the equitable distribution of environmental risks and benefits". This means that all individuals, regardless of their race, color, national origin, or income, should have equal access to environmental benefits and be protected from environmental risks. This definition recognizes the historical and ongoing discrimination faced by marginalized communities in accessing clean air, water, and land, and seeks to address these inequalities.

Some definitions of environmental justice also address procedural justice, which is the "fair and meaningful participation in decision-making". This recognizes the importance of including the perspectives and needs of all individuals in environmental decision-making processes. Marginalized communities, particularly those affected by brownfields, have often been excluded from these processes, leading to decisions that do not adequately address their concerns.

Other scholars emphasize recognition justice, which is the "recognition of oppression" and difference in environmental justice communities. This definition recognizes the historical and ongoing oppression faced by marginalized communities in environmental decision-making and seeks to address these systemic inequalities.

The United States Environmental Protection Agency (EPA) defines environmental justice as:

> the fair treatment and meaningful involvement of all people regardless of race, color, national origin, or income, with respect to the development, implementation, and enforcement of environmental laws, regulations, and policies.

This definition highlights the importance of including all individuals in environmental decision-making and ensuring that these decisions are fair and equitable.

Environmental justice is also discussed as environmental racism or environmental inequality. These terms recognize the disproportionate impact of environmental degradation and pollution on marginalized communities, particularly those in the Global South. This is due to the historical and ongoing exploitation of these communities for natural resources and the resulting environmental degradation.

In the context of brownfields redevelopment, environmental justice is crucial as these properties have the potential to bring significant benefits, such as job creation and improved property values, to surrounding communities. However, if these benefits are not equitably distributed, it can exacerbate existing inequalities and further marginalize already disadvantaged communities.

In the next section, we will explore the concept of equity in brownfields redevelopment and its importance in addressing environmental justice issues.





### Subsection: 6.1b Environmental Justice and Brownfields

Brownfields, or abandoned or underutilized properties with potential environmental contamination, have been a major issue in urban areas for decades. These properties often pose significant health and safety risks to nearby communities, particularly those that are already disadvantaged. The redevelopment of brownfields presents a unique opportunity to address environmental justice concerns and promote equitable development.

#### 6.1b Environmental Justice and Brownfields

The redevelopment of brownfields has been a key focus of environmental justice efforts. These properties, often located in low-income and minority communities, have been neglected and abandoned for years, leaving behind a legacy of environmental contamination. The redevelopment of these properties can bring new economic opportunities and improve the quality of life for these communities, but it must be done in a way that is equitable and just.

One of the key challenges in brownfield redevelopment is ensuring that the benefits of redevelopment are equitably distributed. This includes not only the economic benefits, but also the environmental benefits. For example, the redevelopment of a brownfield into a park or green space can provide much-needed access to nature and recreational opportunities for nearby communities. However, if these benefits are not accessible to all members of the community, particularly those who have been most affected by the brownfield, then the redevelopment is not truly equitable.

In addition to equitable distribution of benefits, it is also important to ensure that the burdens of brownfield redevelopment are not unfairly placed on marginalized communities. This includes considerations of potential health risks during the redevelopment process, as well as potential gentrification and displacement of low-income residents after redevelopment.

The concept of environmental justice also highlights the importance of meaningful community participation in brownfield redevelopment decisions. Marginalized communities, particularly those affected by brownfields, have often been excluded from decision-making processes. This not only perpetuates inequalities, but also leads to redevelopment plans that do not adequately address the needs and concerns of these communities.

In conclusion, brownfield redevelopment presents a unique opportunity to address environmental justice concerns and promote equitable development. By ensuring the equitable distribution of benefits and burdens, and by involving marginalized communities in decision-making processes, we can create more just and sustainable urban environments.

### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the important topic of environmental justice and equity in the context of urban redevelopment. We have discussed the historical and social factors that have led to the unequal distribution of environmental benefits and burdens, and the need for policies and practices that promote equity and justice in the redevelopment of brownfields. We have also examined the role of community engagement and participation in the decision-making process, and the importance of considering the needs and concerns of marginalized communities in the redevelopment of urban areas.

It is clear that environmental justice and equity are crucial considerations in the redevelopment of brownfields. As we move forward, it is essential that we continue to prioritize these issues and work towards creating more equitable and just urban environments for all. This will require a collaborative and inclusive approach, involving all stakeholders and communities, and a commitment to addressing the root causes of environmental injustice.

## Chapter: Chapter 7: Brownfields and Health

### Introduction

Brownfields, abandoned or underutilized properties with potential environmental contamination, have been a significant issue in urban areas for decades. These properties, often located in low-income and minority communities, pose a threat to public health and the environment. The redevelopment of these properties, known as brownfield redevelopment, has become a critical topic in urban planning and policy.

In this chapter, we will delve into the complex relationship between brownfields and health. We will explore the various health risks associated with brownfields, including exposure to hazardous substances and the potential for contamination of groundwater and soil. We will also discuss the potential benefits of brownfield redevelopment, such as improved public health outcomes and revitalized communities.

We will also examine the policies and practices surrounding brownfield redevelopment, including federal and state regulations, as well as innovative approaches to financing and community engagement. By understanding these policies and practices, we can better address the challenges of brownfield redevelopment and promote healthier and more sustainable urban environments.

This chapter aims to provide a comprehensive guide to understanding the complex issues surrounding brownfields and health. By the end, readers will have a deeper understanding of the challenges and opportunities presented by brownfield redevelopment, and the role it plays in creating healthier and more equitable urban environments.




### Subsection: 6.1c Case Studies in Environmental Justice

In this section, we will explore some case studies that highlight the complex and multifaceted nature of environmental justice issues. These case studies will provide real-world examples of the challenges and opportunities that arise in the pursuit of environmental justice.

#### 6.1c Case Studies in Environmental Justice

##### Case Study 1: The Flint Water Crisis

The Flint Water Crisis is a prime example of an environmental justice issue that has garnered significant attention in recent years. In 2014, the city of Flint, Michigan switched its water source from Lake Huron to the Flint River without properly treating the water to prevent pipe corrosion. This led to lead contamination in the drinking water, exposing over 100,000 residents, particularly children, to high levels of lead.

The Flint Water Crisis is a clear example of environmental injustice. The city of Flint is predominantly African American and has a high poverty rate. The decision to switch water sources was made without adequate community input or consideration of the potential health risks. This case highlights the importance of community engagement and participation in environmental decision-making processes.

##### Case Study 2: The Navajo Nation Uranium Contamination

The Navajo Nation in the southwestern United States has been heavily impacted by uranium contamination from mining and milling operations on their land. The Navajo Nation has the highest rate of uranium contamination in the United States, with over 500 abandoned uranium mines and 1,500 abandoned uranium mill tailings sites.

The Navajo Nation Uranium Contamination is a complex environmental justice issue that intersects with issues of indigenous rights and economic inequality. The Navajo Nation was not adequately compensated for the uranium mining on their land, and the contamination has had significant health impacts on the community. This case highlights the need for equitable and just compensation for communities impacted by environmental contamination.

##### Case Study 3: The Environmental Injustices of Hurricane Katrina

Hurricane Katrina, which struck the Gulf Coast of the United States in 2005, disproportionately impacted low-income and African American communities. These communities were more likely to live in flood-prone areas and lacked the resources to evacuate or recover from the storm. The slow response and inadequate relief efforts also disproportionately affected these communities.

The environmental injustices of Hurricane Katrina highlight the intersection of environmental and social injustices. The storm itself was a natural disaster, but the unequal impact of the storm on different communities was a result of systemic inequalities and discrimination. This case underscores the need for equitable and just disaster response and recovery efforts.

These case studies demonstrate the multifaceted nature of environmental justice issues and the importance of addressing them in a comprehensive and equitable manner. They also highlight the need for community engagement and participation in environmental decision-making processes, as well as the importance of equitable compensation for communities impacted by environmental contamination.




#### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the complex and often contentious issue of environmental justice and equity in the context of brownfield redevelopment. We have discussed the historical and social factors that have led to the unequal distribution of environmental hazards and benefits, and the resulting disparities in health and well-being among different communities. We have also examined the role of policy and practice in addressing these issues, and the challenges and opportunities that exist in doing so.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is the importance of considering environmental justice and equity in all aspects of brownfield redevelopment. This includes not only the initial assessment and cleanup of the site, but also the planning and implementation of the redevelopment itself. It is crucial that we strive to ensure that all communities, regardless of their socio-economic status or ethnicity, have equal access to the benefits of brownfield redevelopment, and are not disproportionately burdened by its potential risks.

Another important point to note is the need for collaboration and communication among all stakeholders in brownfield redevelopment. This includes not only government agencies and private developers, but also the local community itself. By involving all stakeholders in the decision-making process, we can ensure that the redevelopment plans are not only environmentally sound, but also socially and economically equitable.

In conclusion, environmental justice and equity are fundamental considerations in brownfield redevelopment. By addressing these issues in a comprehensive and collaborative manner, we can not only revitalize our urban areas, but also create healthier and more equitable communities for all.

### Introduction

Brownfields, abandoned or underutilized properties with real or perceived environmental contamination, pose significant challenges for urban redevelopment. The presence of environmental constraints, such as soil and groundwater contamination, can hinder the revitalization of these properties and limit their potential for future use. However, with the right policies and technologies, these constraints can be effectively managed and overcome, paving the way for successful brownfield redevelopment.

In this chapter, we will delve into the complex world of environmental constraints and cleanup technologies, exploring the various factors that influence the cleanup process and the technologies available for remediation. We will also examine the policies and regulations that govern brownfield cleanup, and how these can impact the redevelopment process.

The chapter will be divided into several sections, each focusing on a specific aspect of environmental constraints and cleanup technologies. We will begin by discussing the different types of environmental constraints commonly found in brownfields, including soil and groundwater contamination, and the potential risks they pose. We will then explore the various cleanup technologies available for addressing these constraints, including physical, chemical, and biological methods.

Next, we will delve into the policies and regulations that govern brownfield cleanup, including federal, state, and local laws. We will discuss how these policies can influence the cleanup process and the technologies that can be used, and how they can impact the overall cost and feasibility of brownfield redevelopment.

Finally, we will examine case studies of successful brownfield redevelopment projects, highlighting the environmental constraints faced and the cleanup technologies used. These case studies will provide valuable insights into the practical application of the concepts discussed in this chapter, and will serve as examples for future brownfield redevelopment projects.

By the end of this chapter, readers will have a comprehensive understanding of the environmental constraints and cleanup technologies involved in brownfield redevelopment. This knowledge will be invaluable for anyone involved in the process, whether as a policy maker, a practitioner, or a community member.




### Subsection: 7.1a Types of Environmental Constraints

Environmental constraints are a major factor in the redevelopment of brownfields. These constraints can take various forms, including soil and groundwater contamination, air pollution, and hazardous waste. Each of these constraints presents unique challenges and requires specific cleanup technologies and policies.

#### Soil and Groundwater Contamination

Soil and groundwater contamination is one of the most common environmental constraints found in brownfields. This contamination can be caused by a variety of sources, including industrial activities, improper waste disposal, and leaking underground storage tanks. The presence of contaminants in the soil and groundwater can pose significant health risks and limit the potential for future use of the property.

Soil and groundwater contamination can be addressed through a variety of cleanup technologies. Physical remediation techniques, such as excavation and removal of contaminated soil, can be used to remove the source of the contamination. Chemical remediation techniques, such as chemical oxidation and bioremediation, can be used to break down contaminants into less harmful substances. Biological remediation techniques, such as phytoremediation and mycoremediation, use plants and fungi to absorb and break down contaminants.

#### Air Pollution

Air pollution is another common environmental constraint found in brownfields. This pollution can be caused by a variety of sources, including industrial processes, combustion of fossil fuels, and improper storage of hazardous materials. Air pollution can have significant impacts on human health and the environment, and can limit the potential for future use of the property.

Air pollution can be addressed through a variety of cleanup technologies. Physical remediation techniques, such as air filtration and scrubbing, can be used to remove pollutants from the air. Chemical remediation techniques, such as chemical absorption and adsorption, can be used to capture and remove pollutants from the air. Biological remediation techniques, such as biofiltration and bioremediation, use microorganisms to break down pollutants into less harmful substances.

#### Hazardous Waste

Hazardous waste is a third common environmental constraint found in brownfields. This waste can be generated from a variety of sources, including industrial processes, household products, and medical waste. Hazardous waste can pose significant health risks and limit the potential for future use of the property.

Hazardous waste can be addressed through a variety of cleanup technologies. Physical remediation techniques, such as incineration and melting, can be used to destroy hazardous waste. Chemical remediation techniques, such as chemical precipitation and neutralization, can be used to transform hazardous waste into less harmful substances. Biological remediation techniques, such as composting and bioremediation, use microorganisms to break down hazardous waste into less harmful substances.

In the next section, we will delve deeper into the policies and regulations that govern the cleanup of these environmental constraints, and how they can impact the redevelopment of brownfields.




### Subsection: 7.1b Impact on Redevelopment

Environmental constraints have a significant impact on the redevelopment of brownfields. These constraints can limit the potential for future use of the property and pose significant challenges for developers and urban planners. However, with the right policies and cleanup technologies, these constraints can be addressed and the property can be redeveloped for productive use.

#### Soil and Groundwater Contamination

Soil and groundwater contamination can have a significant impact on the redevelopment of brownfields. The presence of contaminants in the soil and groundwater can pose health risks to future occupants and limit the potential for future use of the property. This can be particularly problematic for urban redevelopment, where the potential for contamination is high due to the presence of industrial activities and improper waste disposal.

However, with the right cleanup technologies, soil and groundwater contamination can be addressed. Physical remediation techniques, such as excavation and removal of contaminated soil, can be used to remove the source of the contamination. Chemical remediation techniques, such as chemical oxidation and bioremediation, can be used to break down contaminants into less harmful substances. Biological remediation techniques, such as phytoremediation and mycoremediation, use plants and fungi to absorb and break down contaminants.

#### Air Pollution

Air pollution is another significant environmental constraint that can impact the redevelopment of brownfields. Air pollution can pose health risks to future occupants and limit the potential for future use of the property. This is particularly true for urban redevelopment, where the potential for air pollution is high due to the presence of industrial processes and combustion of fossil fuels.

However, with the right policies and cleanup technologies, air pollution can be addressed. Physical remediation techniques, such as air filtration and scrubbing, can be used to remove pollutants from the air. Chemical remediation techniques, such as chemical absorption and adsorption, can be used to remove pollutants from the air. Biological remediation techniques, such as biofiltration and bioremediation, use microorganisms to break down pollutants into less harmful substances.

In conclusion, environmental constraints play a significant role in the redevelopment of brownfields. However, with the right policies and cleanup technologies, these constraints can be addressed and the property can be redeveloped for productive use. It is important for urban planners and developers to consider these constraints and develop strategies to address them in order to successfully redevelop brownfields.





### Subsection: 7.1c Overcoming Environmental Constraints

Overcoming environmental constraints is crucial for the successful redevelopment of brownfields. It requires a comprehensive understanding of the constraints and the implementation of appropriate cleanup technologies. In this section, we will discuss some strategies for overcoming environmental constraints in urban redevelopment.

#### Policy and Regulation

Policy and regulation play a significant role in overcoming environmental constraints. Governments at all levels have implemented policies and regulations to protect public health and the environment. These policies and regulations provide guidelines for the cleanup of brownfields and the prevention of future contamination. For example, the Comprehensive Environmental Response, Compensation, and Liability Act (CERCLA) in the United States provides a legal framework for the cleanup of hazardous waste sites, including brownfields.

#### Cleanup Technologies

Cleanup technologies are essential for addressing environmental constraints. These technologies can be physical, chemical, or biological, depending on the type of contamination present. Physical remediation techniques, such as excavation and removal of contaminated soil, can be used to remove the source of the contamination. Chemical remediation techniques, such as chemical oxidation and bioremediation, can be used to break down contaminants into less harmful substances. Biological remediation techniques, such as phytoremediation and mycoremediation, use plants and fungi to absorb and break down contaminants.

#### Community Engagement

Community engagement is crucial for overcoming environmental constraints. Brownfields are often located in urban areas, and their redevelopment can have a significant impact on the surrounding community. Therefore, it is essential to involve the community in the planning and implementation of redevelopment projects. This can help address concerns and ensure that the redevelopment is beneficial to the community.

#### Sustainable Design

Sustainable design is another strategy for overcoming environmental constraints. This involves incorporating sustainable practices into the design and construction of buildings and infrastructure. For example, using green roofs, which can absorb rainwater and reduce the urban heat island effect, can help mitigate the environmental impact of urban redevelopment.

In conclusion, overcoming environmental constraints is crucial for the successful redevelopment of brownfields. It requires a comprehensive understanding of the constraints and the implementation of appropriate cleanup technologies. Policy and regulation, community engagement, and sustainable design are all essential strategies for addressing environmental constraints.

### Subsection: 7.3a Purpose of Risk Assessments

Risk assessments are an essential component of brownfield redevelopment. They provide a systematic approach to understanding and managing the potential risks associated with the redevelopment of a brownfield site. The purpose of risk assessments is to identify, analyze, and evaluate the potential risks that may arise during the redevelopment process. This information is crucial for decision-making and planning, as it allows for the development of strategies to mitigate or eliminate these risks.

Risk assessments are typically conducted by environmental consultants or other professionals with expertise in this area. They involve a thorough investigation of the site, including a review of historical records, site inspections, and soil and groundwater sampling. The results of the risk assessment are then used to develop a risk management plan, which outlines the steps that will be taken to address the identified risks.

The purpose of risk assessments in brownfield redevelopment is multifaceted. It serves to:

1. Identify potential risks: Risk assessments help to identify potential risks that may arise during the redevelopment process. These risks may include contamination of soil or groundwater, exposure to hazardous substances, or potential liability issues.

2. Inform decision-making: The results of risk assessments provide valuable information for decision-making and planning. They help to inform the selection of cleanup technologies, the development of risk management plans, and the allocation of resources.

3. Facilitate compliance: Risk assessments are often required by regulatory agencies as part of the redevelopment process. They help to ensure that the redevelopment is conducted in a manner that complies with all relevant environmental regulations.

4. Mitigate potential impacts: By identifying potential risks early in the redevelopment process, risk assessments allow for the development of strategies to mitigate or eliminate these risks. This can help to minimize potential impacts on the environment and public health.

5. Demonstrate due diligence: Conducting risk assessments can demonstrate due diligence on the part of the redeveloper. This can be important in terms of liability and legal responsibility for any potential contamination or other environmental issues that may arise during the redevelopment process.

In conclusion, risk assessments are a crucial component of brownfield redevelopment. They provide a systematic approach to understanding and managing the potential risks associated with the redevelopment process. By conducting risk assessments, redevelopers can ensure that the redevelopment is conducted in a manner that is safe, compliant, and sustainable.





### Subsection: 7.3b Conducting a Risk Assessment

Conducting a risk assessment for brownfield redevelopment is a complex process that requires a thorough understanding of environmental regulations, cleanup technologies, and potential risks. The following steps outline the process of conducting a risk assessment for brownfield redevelopment:

1. **Site Investigation:** The first step in conducting a risk assessment is to conduct a thorough site investigation. This involves reviewing historical records, conducting site inspections, and collecting soil and groundwater samples. The goal of this investigation is to identify potential sources of contamination and understand the extent of the contamination.

2. **Risk Identification:** Once the site investigation is complete, the next step is to identify potential risks. This involves considering the type of contamination present, the potential impacts of the contamination, and the potential for exposure to the contamination.

3. **Risk Analysis:** After identifying potential risks, the next step is to analyze these risks. This involves determining the likelihood of the risk occurring and the potential severity of the impact. This can be done using various risk assessment tools and models.

4. **Risk Evaluation:** The risk evaluation step involves comparing the results of the risk analysis to regulatory standards and guidelines. This helps to determine if the risks are acceptable or if further mitigation is necessary.

5. **Risk Management:** Based on the results of the risk evaluation, a risk management plan is developed. This plan outlines the steps that will be taken to address the identified risks. This may include the selection of cleanup technologies, the development of safety protocols, or the implementation of monitoring programs.

6. **Monitoring and Review:** The final step in the risk assessment process is to monitor and review the effectiveness of the risk management plan. This involves conducting regular inspections, testing, and audits to ensure that the risks are being effectively managed.

By following these steps, a comprehensive risk assessment can be conducted for brownfield redevelopment. This process helps to ensure that the redevelopment is conducted in a manner that is safe for the community and compliant with environmental regulations. 





### Subsection: 7.3c Interpreting Risk Assessment Results

Interpreting risk assessment results is a crucial step in the brownfield redevelopment process. It involves analyzing the data collected during the risk assessment and using it to inform decision-making. This section will discuss the key steps involved in interpreting risk assessment results.

#### 7.3c.1 Understanding the Data

The first step in interpreting risk assessment results is to understand the data collected during the risk assessment. This includes understanding the type of data collected, the methods used to collect it, and the limitations of the data. For example, if soil samples were collected using a drill rig, it is important to understand the depth and location of the samples, as well as any potential contamination in the drill rig itself.

#### 7.3c.2 Identifying Key Findings

Once the data is understood, the next step is to identify key findings. This involves identifying the most significant sources of contamination, the potential impacts of the contamination, and the potential for exposure to the contamination. These key findings will inform the risk management plan and help prioritize cleanup efforts.

#### 7.3c.3 Comparing to Regulatory Standards

After identifying key findings, the next step is to compare them to regulatory standards and guidelines. This helps to determine if the risks are acceptable or if further mitigation is necessary. For example, if the risk assessment results show that the soil contamination levels exceed regulatory standards, further cleanup efforts will be necessary.

#### 7.3c.4 Developing a Risk Management Plan

Based on the key findings and comparison to regulatory standards, a risk management plan can be developed. This plan outlines the steps that will be taken to address the identified risks. This may include the selection of cleanup technologies, the development of safety protocols, or the implementation of monitoring programs.

#### 7.3c.5 Monitoring and Review

The final step in interpreting risk assessment results is to monitor and review the effectiveness of the risk management plan. This involves conducting regular inspections and testing to ensure that the cleanup efforts are working as intended. If necessary, the risk management plan can be adjusted to address any new findings or changes in the risk assessment results.

In conclusion, interpreting risk assessment results is a crucial step in the brownfield redevelopment process. It involves understanding the data, identifying key findings, comparing to regulatory standards, developing a risk management plan, and monitoring and reviewing the effectiveness of the plan. By following these steps, brownfield redevelopment projects can effectively address environmental constraints and ensure the successful cleanup and reuse of these sites.





### Subsection: 7.4 Guest Speaker - Dave Merill:

#### 7.4a Dave Merill's Background

Dave Merill is a renowned environmental consultant with over 20 years of experience in the field of brownfield redevelopment. He has worked on numerous projects across the United States, helping to transform contaminated sites into productive urban spaces. Merill's expertise lies in the areas of risk assessment, cleanup technologies, and policy development.

Merill's career began in the early 1990s when he joined a small environmental consulting firm in Boston. There, he worked on his first brownfield redevelopment project, a former industrial site in the city's South Station neighborhood. The project, which involved the cleanup of heavy metal contamination, sparked Merill's interest in the field and set the course for his future career.

In the late 1990s, Merill joined a larger environmental consulting firm, where he worked on a variety of brownfield redevelopment projects across the United States. During this time, he developed a deep understanding of the complexities of brownfield redevelopment, including the technical, regulatory, and policy aspects.

In 2005, Merill founded his own environmental consulting firm, Merill Environmental Consulting (MEC). MEC has since become a leading firm in the field of brownfield redevelopment, with a focus on risk assessment, cleanup technologies, and policy development.

Merill's work has been recognized by numerous industry organizations, including the Environmental Protection Agency (EPA) and the National Brownfields Training Conference. He has also been a guest speaker at numerous conferences and universities, sharing his expertise and insights on brownfield redevelopment.

In addition to his work as a consultant, Merill is also a published author. His book, "Brownfield Redevelopment: A Comprehensive Guide to Urban Redevelopment," is a highly regarded resource for students and professionals in the field.

Merill's background and expertise make him a valuable guest speaker for this chapter on environmental constraints and cleanup technologies. His insights and experiences will provide students with a deeper understanding of the complexities of brownfield redevelopment and the role of cleanup technologies in the process.

#### 7.4b Merill's Work in Brownfield Redevelopment

Dave Merill's work in brownfield redevelopment has been instrumental in transforming contaminated sites into productive urban spaces. His expertise in risk assessment, cleanup technologies, and policy development has been crucial in the successful redevelopment of numerous brownfield sites across the United States.

One of Merill's most notable projects is the redevelopment of the former Bethlehem Steel site in Lackawanna, New York. The site, which was once a major steel production facility, had been abandoned for over a decade and was heavily contaminated with various hazardous substances. Merill's team was tasked with conducting a comprehensive risk assessment of the site, which involved collecting and analyzing soil, groundwater, and air samples. The risk assessment results were then used to develop a cleanup plan that involved the removal and disposal of contaminated soil and groundwater, as well as the implementation of institutional controls to prevent future contamination.

Another significant project led by Merill was the redevelopment of the former Naval Air Station Alameda in California. The site, which was once a naval base, had been abandoned for over 20 years and was heavily contaminated with various hazardous substances, including petroleum hydrocarbons and heavy metals. Merill's team was responsible for conducting a risk assessment of the site and developing a cleanup plan that involved the removal and disposal of contaminated soil and groundwater, as well as the implementation of institutional controls. The project also involved the remediation of a former landfill on the site, which required the use of advanced cleanup technologies such as bioremediation and phytoremediation.

Merill's work in brownfield redevelopment has not only transformed contaminated sites into productive urban spaces but has also contributed to the development of policies and regulations related to brownfield redevelopment. His expertise has been sought after by various government agencies and organizations, including the EPA and the National Brownfields Training Conference. Merill has also been a guest speaker at numerous conferences and universities, sharing his insights and experiences on brownfield redevelopment.

In conclusion, Dave Merill's work in brownfield redevelopment has been a significant contribution to the field. His expertise and dedication have helped transform contaminated sites into productive urban spaces, and his contributions to policy development have been instrumental in the successful redevelopment of brownfield sites across the United States.

## Chapter: Brownfields Policy and Practice: A Comprehensive Guide to Urban Redevelopment




### Introduction

In this chapter, we will be recapping the various environmental issues that have been discussed throughout this book. As we have seen, brownfields pose a significant challenge to urban redevelopment due to the presence of environmental contamination. This chapter will serve as a comprehensive guide to understanding the environmental issues associated with brownfields and how they can be addressed.

We will begin by revisiting the definition of brownfields and the types of contamination that can be found on these sites. Brownfields are abandoned or underutilized properties that have been contaminated by hazardous substances, pollutants, or other contaminants. These contaminants can pose serious health risks to humans and the environment, making it necessary to address them before redevelopment can take place.

Next, we will delve into the various policies and regulations that have been put in place to address brownfields. These policies and regulations are constantly evolving as new technologies and methods for remediation are developed. Some of the key federal, state, and local laws that we will discuss include the Comprehensive Environmental Response, Compensation, and Liability Act (CERCLA), the Brownfields Revitalization and Environmental Restoration Act, and the Massachusetts Brownfields Law.

We will also explore the different stakeholders involved in brownfield redevelopment, such as government agencies, developers, and community members. Each stakeholder plays a crucial role in the process, and it is important to understand their perspectives and concerns in order to successfully navigate the complexities of brownfield redevelopment.

Next, we will discuss the various methods and technologies used for brownfield remediation. These include traditional methods such as excavation and soil capping, as well as more innovative techniques such as phytoremediation and bioremediation. We will also touch upon the economic considerations of brownfield redevelopment, including the costs associated with cleanup and the potential benefits of redevelopment.

Finally, we will examine case studies of successful brownfield redevelopment projects, highlighting the strategies and approaches used to overcome environmental challenges and achieve successful outcomes. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a comprehensive understanding of the environmental issues associated with brownfields and the policies, practices, and technologies used to address them.


## Chapter: Brownfields Policy and Practice: A Comprehensive Guide to Urban Redevelopment




### Subsection: 8.1b Impact on Redevelopment

The redevelopment of brownfields has a significant impact on the surrounding community and the environment. The process of redeveloping brownfields involves the cleanup and remediation of contaminated sites, which can have both positive and negative effects on the surrounding area.

#### Positive Impacts

The redevelopment of brownfields can have several positive impacts on the surrounding community. One of the most significant benefits is the creation of new housing opportunities. As seen in the case of New Columbia, the redevelopment of brownfields can result in the construction of new housing units, providing much-needed affordable housing options for low-income residents. This can help alleviate housing shortages and improve the quality of life for residents.

Moreover, the redevelopment of brownfields can also lead to the creation of new jobs. The process of cleanup and remediation requires skilled labor, and the construction of new housing units or other developments can create job opportunities in the construction industry. This can help stimulate the local economy and provide employment opportunities for residents.

#### Negative Impacts

While the redevelopment of brownfields can have positive impacts, it can also have negative effects on the surrounding community. One of the main concerns is the potential displacement of residents. As seen in the case of New Columbia, the redevelopment process can require residents to relocate temporarily or permanently, which can be disruptive and cause hardship for residents.

Furthermore, the redevelopment of brownfields can also have environmental impacts. The cleanup and remediation process can involve the use of hazardous materials and chemicals, which can have negative effects on the surrounding environment. It is essential to carefully consider and mitigate these potential impacts to minimize harm to the environment.

#### Conclusion

In conclusion, the redevelopment of brownfields has a significant impact on the surrounding community and the environment. While it can provide benefits such as new housing opportunities and job creation, it is crucial to carefully consider and mitigate potential negative impacts to ensure the well-being of the community and the environment. The process of redevelopment should involve collaboration and communication between all stakeholders, including residents, government agencies, and developers, to ensure a successful and sustainable outcome.





### Subsection: 8.1c Future Trends in Environmental Constraints

As we continue to face environmental challenges, it is crucial to consider the future trends in environmental constraints that may impact urban redevelopment. These trends include the increasing frequency and severity of natural disasters, the rise of greenhouse gas emissions, and the depletion of natural resources.

#### Natural Disasters

The frequency and severity of natural disasters, such as hurricanes, floods, and wildfires, are expected to increase in the coming years. These disasters can have devastating effects on urban areas, causing significant damage to infrastructure and displacing residents. As we continue to develop and redevelop urban areas, it is essential to consider the potential impact of these natural disasters and incorporate disaster-resilient design principles into our plans.

#### Greenhouse Gas Emissions

The rise of greenhouse gas emissions is another significant environmental constraint that will continue to impact urban redevelopment. As mentioned in the previous section, the average global temperature is expected to rise by more than two degrees, causing serious problems such as sea level rise, extreme weather events, and loss of biodiversity. To mitigate these effects, urban redevelopment plans must prioritize energy efficiency and the use of renewable energy sources.

#### Depletion of Natural Resources

The depletion of natural resources, such as water and minerals, is also a significant concern for urban redevelopment. As our population continues to grow, the demand for these resources will only increase, putting pressure on already limited supplies. Urban redevelopment plans must consider sustainable resource management practices to ensure the long-term availability of these resources.

#### Urban Mining

As mentioned in the related context, the concept of "urban mining" is becoming increasingly relevant as cities become richer sources of raw materials for metal than mineral deposits in nature. This trend will continue to impact urban redevelopment, as cities will need to find ways to efficiently and sustainably extract these resources.

#### Parks as Refuges

As our natural resources become depleted, parks and other green spaces will become increasingly important as refuges for nature. As seen in the related context, zoos have already become the last refuge for many endangered species. Similarly, parks will need to be protected and managed to preserve biodiversity and provide a refuge for nature in urban areas.

#### The Role of Technology

Advancements in technology, such as artificial intelligence and the Internet of Things, will also play a significant role in future trends in environmental constraints. These technologies can help us better understand and manage our environment, but they can also have unintended consequences, such as increased energy consumption and waste generation. As we continue to incorporate these technologies into our urban redevelopment plans, it is essential to consider their potential environmental impacts.

In conclusion, as we continue to face environmental challenges, it is crucial to consider these future trends in environmental constraints and incorporate them into our urban redevelopment plans. By prioritizing sustainability and resilience, we can ensure the long-term viability of our urban areas and create a better future for all.





#### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the various environmental issues that are associated with brownfield redevelopment. We have discussed the importance of understanding these issues and the potential impacts they can have on the surrounding community. We have also examined the role of policy and practice in addressing these issues and promoting sustainable redevelopment.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is the importance of conducting thorough environmental assessments before beginning any brownfield redevelopment project. This includes assessing the site for potential contamination, as well as understanding the local ecosystem and potential impacts on biodiversity. By conducting these assessments, developers can better understand the potential risks and develop strategies to mitigate them.

Another important aspect of brownfield redevelopment is the use of sustainable practices. This includes incorporating green infrastructure, such as rain gardens and permeable pavement, to help manage stormwater runoff and reduce the impact on local water bodies. It also involves using sustainable building materials and construction techniques to minimize the environmental impact of the redevelopment.

Policy plays a crucial role in promoting sustainable brownfield redevelopment. Governments at all levels have implemented policies and regulations to encourage the cleanup and redevelopment of brownfields. These policies provide incentives, such as tax breaks and grants, to developers who choose to redevelop brownfields instead of greenfields. They also set standards and guidelines for environmental assessments and remediation, ensuring that brownfield redevelopment is done in a responsible and sustainable manner.

In conclusion, brownfield redevelopment is a complex and multifaceted issue that requires careful consideration of environmental issues, sustainable practices, and policy. By understanding and addressing these issues, we can promote the revitalization of urban areas and create healthier and more sustainable communities.

## Chapter 9: Brownfields Redevelopment:




### Introduction

Brownfields redevelopment is a complex and multifaceted process that requires careful consideration of various economic factors. In this chapter, we will explore the economic considerations that are crucial to the successful redevelopment of brownfields. We will delve into the financial aspects of brownfields redevelopment, including the costs associated with cleanup and remediation, as well as the potential benefits and incentives that can be gained through the process. Additionally, we will examine the role of economic analysis in brownfields redevelopment, and how it can be used to inform decision-making and ensure the viability of a project.

Brownfields redevelopment is a crucial aspect of urban revitalization, as it allows for the transformation of abandoned or underutilized properties into productive and valuable spaces. However, the process is not without its challenges. The presence of contamination and pollution on these sites can pose significant financial and environmental risks, making it essential to carefully consider the economic implications of brownfields redevelopment.

In this chapter, we will also explore the various stakeholders involved in brownfields redevelopment, including developers, investors, and government agencies. Each of these stakeholders has a unique role to play in the process, and understanding their perspectives and interests is crucial for successful brownfields redevelopment.

Overall, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive guide to the economic considerations in brownfields redevelopment. By the end, readers will have a better understanding of the financial aspects of brownfields redevelopment, as well as the role of economic analysis in the process. This knowledge will be valuable for anyone involved in brownfields redevelopment, whether as a developer, investor, or government official. 





#### 9.1a Cost-Benefit Analysis

Cost-benefit analysis (CBA) is a systematic approach to estimating the strengths and weaknesses of alternatives in terms of their costs and benefits. It is a crucial tool in the process of brownfields redevelopment, as it allows for a comprehensive evaluation of the economic implications of different redevelopment strategies.

CBA is based on the principle of Pareto optimality, which states that a project is considered beneficial if it results in a net gain in welfare for at least one individual, without causing a net loss in welfare for any other individual. This principle is used to evaluate the overall impact of a project on society, taking into account both the direct and indirect effects of the project.

The process of CBA involves identifying and quantifying the costs and benefits associated with a project. Costs may include cleanup and remediation expenses, as well as any potential legal or regulatory fees. Benefits may include increased property values, job creation, and improved environmental conditions. These costs and benefits are then compared to determine the net benefit of the project.

One of the key advantages of CBA is that it allows for a comparison of different redevelopment strategies based on their economic impacts. This can help decision-makers choose the most cost-effective and beneficial option for the community.

However, CBA also has its limitations. It relies heavily on assumptions and projections, which may not always be accurate. It also does not take into account non-economic factors, such as social or environmental impacts, which may be important considerations in brownfields redevelopment.

Despite its limitations, CBA remains a valuable tool in the process of brownfields redevelopment. It provides a systematic and objective way to evaluate the economic implications of different strategies, and can help guide decision-making towards the most beneficial outcome for the community.





#### 9.1b Financing Redevelopment

Financing is a crucial aspect of brownfields redevelopment, as it can greatly impact the success and sustainability of a project. In this section, we will discuss the various financing options available for brownfields redevelopment and their advantages and disadvantages.

One of the main financing options for brownfields redevelopment is through public funding. This can come from federal, state, or local governments and can include grants, loans, or tax incentives. Public funding can be a valuable resource for brownfields redevelopment, as it can help offset the high costs associated with cleanup and remediation. However, it also comes with strict regulations and may not always be available for every project.

Another financing option is through private funding, which can come from individual investors, venture capitalists, or private equity firms. Private funding can be a more flexible and less bureaucratic option compared to public funding, but it also comes with higher interest rates and may require a more significant equity stake in the project.

In addition to traditional financing options, there are also specialized programs and funds available for brownfields redevelopment. These can include brownfields tax incentives, which allow for the deduction of cleanup costs from taxes, and brownfields revolving loans, which provide low-interest loans for cleanup and redevelopment. These programs can be a valuable resource for brownfields redevelopment, but they may also have specific eligibility requirements and may not always be available for every project.

It is important for developers and investors to carefully consider the financing options available for brownfields redevelopment and to weigh the advantages and disadvantages of each. By understanding the financing options and their implications, developers and investors can make informed decisions and increase the chances of success for their brownfields redevelopment projects.





#### 9.1c Economic Impact of Redevelopment

The economic impact of brownfields redevelopment is a crucial consideration for any project. It refers to the changes in economic activity and conditions that result from the cleanup and redevelopment of a brownfield site. These impacts can be positive or negative and can have a significant impact on the surrounding community and the overall economy.

One of the main positive economic impacts of brownfields redevelopment is job creation. The cleanup and redevelopment of a brownfield site can create jobs in various industries, including construction, environmental consulting, and retail. These jobs can provide employment opportunities for local residents and help stimulate the local economy. Additionally, the redevelopment of a brownfield site can also attract new businesses and industries to the area, further creating job opportunities and boosting the local economy.

Another positive economic impact of brownfields redevelopment is increased property values. The cleanup and redevelopment of a brownfield site can lead to an increase in property values in the surrounding area. This can be especially beneficial for nearby property owners, as it can increase their property values and potentially provide them with additional revenue. However, it is important to note that the increase in property values may also lead to gentrification and displacement of low-income residents in some cases.

On the other hand, there can also be negative economic impacts of brownfields redevelopment. One of the main concerns is the potential for increased taxes. The cleanup and redevelopment of a brownfield site can lead to an increase in property taxes, which can be a burden for both property owners and the local government. Additionally, the redevelopment of a brownfield site can also lead to increased traffic and congestion, which can have a negative impact on the surrounding community.

It is important for developers and investors to carefully consider the potential economic impacts of brownfields redevelopment and to work closely with the local community to mitigate any potential negative impacts. By understanding and addressing these economic considerations, brownfields redevelopment can be a valuable tool for urban revitalization and economic growth.
